市商會痛陳裁厘後意見 119

Opinions of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce after the abolition of Likin

Road Goods Tax and Postal Parcel Tax Should Be Abolished Simultaneously

Rectification of Resolutions of the Five-Province Conference on Likin Abolition

Business Tax Rate Should Not Exceed Two Per Thousand

The Fourth Plenary Session of the Kuomintang decided to abolish Likin on January 1, 1931. The Ministry of Finance is currently rushing to complete various procedures to ensure its implementation on schedule without delay. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency, considering this matter of great importance to the business community, interviewed Mr. Tu Xiaolai, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, to inquire about the Chamber's opinions on the implementation of Likin abolition. According to Mr. Wang, merchants have long yearned for the abolition of Likin. They are delighted that the government can resolutely implement it. However, whether the abolition will be thorough and how to remedy it are also matters of great concern. Therefore, the Chamber of Commerce specifically tasked the Standing Committee members Tu Yansong, Xu Ji, Ye Huijun, Yuan Ludeng, the Head of the General Affairs Section Fang Jiaobo, the Director of the General Affairs Section Luo Qinghua, the Secretary Yan Ersheng, and the Secretary-General Xiang Chengqing to conduct a detailed study and decided to make a thorough and urgent request to the Ministry of Finance to enable merchants to benefit from the resolution of the Fourth Plenary Session, and to send letters to Chambers of Commerce in all provinces, cities, and counties to ensure a consistent position. The original text is as follows:

Document to the Ministry of Finance: A petition for urgent and detailed planning regarding the abolition of Likin and compensatory measures to avoid negative consequences. We humbly submit our opinions for your review and implementation. The abolition of Likin has been repeatedly ordered and scheduled for implementation since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, but has been suspended due to frequent military conflicts. Recently, with the gradual pacification of You, Yan, Bian, and Luo, the Fourth Plenary Session decided to implement Likin abolition on January 1, 1931. This resolution, weighing the situation, is unlikely to change. This is indeed a great opportunity for merchants to look forward to sweeping away cumbersome taxes and removing long-hanging burdens. However, considering that hundreds of thousands of people are involved in Likin, and that the national finances are strained and in dire need of resources after the military conflicts, it is imperative to plan for compensatory measures. We fear that hasty planning may lead to unintended consequences, where the disadvantages outweigh the advantages. This would be contrary to the government's intention to start afresh with the people and the merchants' initial hope for Likin abolition. Therefore, we dare to offer our humble opinions for the Ministry's consideration. The so-called Likin taxes had specific names and established procedures. However, provinces later acted independently, focusing on maximizing revenue to expand their armies and enrich themselves. As a result, the newly added taxes were bizarre and unfamiliar, making it difficult for merchants from other provinces to understand and even for the Ministry to keep track of. Taking the recent case of the Wing On Textile Company transporting goods to Chongqing and requesting exemption from double taxation as an example, the Provincial Department of Finance replied to the Ministry stating that they had strictly ordered the tax bureaus to prevent double taxation. However, the 21st Army Commander of the province, in his reply to the Chongqing General Chamber of Commerce on behalf of the company's request, stated that the company should be exempt from the Chongqing Consolidated Tax, following the example of the Hubei Yuhua Textile Company, but that all other pooled taxes should be paid. The so-called Chongqing Consolidated Tax is the province's official Likin, while the other taxes are the province's privately added Likin. The phrase "other taxes" clearly demonstrates the multitude of names and the complexity of the types of taxes, which burden merchants many times more than Likin itself. Previously, machine-made imitation foreign goods, after paying export tax, could pass through the entire country without being subject to any further taxes, except for the Chongwen Dou Tax Bureau. However, now, after several months, the Provincial Department of Finance's reply to the Ministry is outwardly compliant, but in reality, the province has its own tax regulations. The Ministry's regulations on exempting machine-made foreign goods from double taxation have long been disregarded in the reply to the Chongqing Chamber of Commerce, citing only Sichuan Province as an example. Other similar cases are too numerous to mention. We fear that after Likin abolition, only the officially reported Likin will be abolished, while the other privately added, bizarrely named taxes, similar to Likin, will continue to exist, with the Ministry having no records to rely on. Other provinces may rely on this as a source of revenue, either concealing it or protecting it by any means. In this case, merchants will not receive the benefits of Likin abolition and will instead face additional burdens. Therefore, we urge the Ministry to take swift and decisive action to thoroughly eliminate these taxes. First, the Ministry must bring the finances of all provinces back on track to prevent them from protecting Likin in disguise. Only then can the true purpose of Likin abolition be achieved. This is our first request. The abolition of Likin should include all taxes similar in nature to transit taxes. According to the resolution of the previous Likin Abolition Conference, the following should be abolished in addition to Likin: (1) Railway Goods Tax, (2) Postal Parcel Tax, (3) Customs Duties and surcharges beyond ten li of the business port, (4) Import Duties and surcharges of new maritime and land customs, (5) Re-import Duties and surcharges of new maritime and land customs, (6) Export Duties and surcharges of new maritime and land customs from this port to that port, (7) Customs Duties and surcharges within fifty li of the business port. The current implementation of Likin abolition is to complete the unfinished work of the previous Likin Abolition Conference. All previous resolutions, which accommodated the requests of the business community and were carefully formulated, should be adhered to. We urge the Ministry to abolish Likin, Goods Tax, and Landing Tax on January 1 of next year. The remaining seven similar taxes, excluding items three to seven, should be abolished in stages following the previous resolution. The Railway Goods Tax and Postal Parcel Tax, which are most harmful to businesses, should be abolished simultaneously on January 1 of next year to ensure the early implementation of policies that benefit businesses. This is our second request. Next is the issue of compensatory measures. The discussion of Likin abolition in our country began in the Renyin year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty. The proposed compensatory measures included increasing import duties to 2.5% of the value, and the remaining measures only included production and sales taxes and factory taxes, which are similar to the special consumption taxes discussed recently. Currently, the most important import tariff, based on the current tariff rates, is already 27.5% of the value, and we have heard that the upcoming revised tariff rates will also have some increases, which is more than double the old treaty of Renyin. In addition, according to the resolution of the previous Likin Abolition Conference, there are also business taxes and special consumption taxes as compensatory measures. This should be more than enough to make up for the shortfall. Merchants hope that Likin abolition will reduce their burden. If there are any short-sighted individuals who propose levying new types of taxes as compensatory measures, we urge the Ministry to consider the people's hardships and not adopt such proposals. This is our third request. The main points of the guidelines for the implementation of special consumption taxes, as resolved in the previous conference, are: (1) One tax per item, such as refunding the cocoon tax after paying the silk tax; (2) One tax valid nationwide; (3) The tax rate for special consumption taxes in place of Likin should not be higher than the original tax rate; (4) Taxes must be levied on the major products of the region; otherwise, no taxes should be levied. Only by adhering to these four principles can we avoid disguised and intensified taxes. Among the provinces that implemented special consumption taxes earlier, Jiangxi and Fujian provinces were at the forefront. However, judging from the current situation in these two provinces, the hardships of the merchants have worsened compared to before the abolition of Likin. Taking the Jiangxi Finance Special Commissioner's Office's reply to the Jiangxi Chamber of Commerce Federation in November of the 18th year as an example, after examining it item by item, it can be seen that the province has not fully implemented the refund of double taxation. For example, regarding oil producers, if they produce oil from soybeans, once a tax refund is issued, it will inevitably lead to mutual borrowing of tax tickets and other malpractices, as stated in the strict reply. Goods imported from other provinces and not sold in Jiangxi Province are still required to pay taxes. This is tantamount to completely overturning the principles established in the implementation guidelines for special consumption taxes. On the one hand, the province is using the name of consumption tax to increase tax rates to over 15% of the value. All these situations show that merchants have not benefited from Likin abolition and have instead suffered from the harm of Likin abolition. We will not discuss the completed cases of Jiangxi and Fujian for the time being and will instead study the resolution of the Five-Province Conference on Likin Abolition. Item Ren of the resolution states that when collecting special taxes and consumption taxes, goods that are easy to produce and sell and levy taxes at the same time should be levied at once. However, if it is more convenient to levy taxes separately, methods can also be devised to levy taxes separately. This leaves room for future tax cards and difficulties. The provision in the implementation guidelines for special consumption taxes that one tax is valid nationwide is considered worthless. Although Likin tax rates varied from province to province in the past, they were mostly between 2% and 5%. The name "Likin" itself implies that the ratio should not be too high. Although the total tax rate for goods passing through several provinces sometimes reached 20% or 30%, the tax rate for goods sold only in the province or nearby provinces was not very high. The implementation guidelines for special consumption taxes clearly stipulate that after changing to special taxes, the tax rate should not exceed the original tax rate, although there is a clause stating that luxury goods are not subject to this rule. However, there is room for deliberation on the categories and tax rates. This is why the implementation guidelines for special consumption taxes stipulate that the financial authorities must consult with commercial organizations before deciding on the collection method of special consumption taxes. However, the Five-Province Conference on Likin Abolition hastily decided on a maximum tax rate of 17.5% of the value based solely on the opinions of government officials. The determination of what constitutes luxury goods and semi-luxury goods is entirely based on the reports and verification of each province, without any input from commercial organizations. This is in stark contrast to the guidelines. The implementation guidelines for special consumption taxes stipulate that each place that must levy taxes can only set up one consumer tax bureau to preside over the matter and must not set up a bureau for each category of goods. However, the Five-Province Conference on Likin Abolition has implicitly changed this rule. Goods of the same nature and with similar collection procedures, as well as goods with small amounts of revenue, should be taxed in the same place and managed by one bureau. However, in the initial stage, large quantities of goods can also be taxed according to category. According to the above regulations, oil and seafood, wood and livestock are not of the same nature and can always be taxed according to category. More agencies mean more expenses for the government, and more categories of bureaus mean more inspections for merchants, which is more troublesome than the previous unified collection and inspection of all kinds of Likin. In short, the implementation guidelines for special consumption taxes were formulated by the government after accommodating the opinions of the business community during the Likin Abolition Conference. After careful consideration, there were good points. However, once the Five-Province Conference on Likin Abolition made implicit changes, all the good points were virtually abolished. Therefore, the reform of special taxes in other provinces feels more painful than Likin. Learning from the past, we are truly frightened. The reform of special taxes in this Likin abolition is not comparable to the partial trials in Jiangxi and other provinces. The impact on the entire country will be significant if we are not careful. We urge the Ministry to strictly implement the guidelines for special consumption taxes. All resolutions of the Five-Province Conference on Likin Abolition that conflict with these guidelines should be abolished and rectified. The most important ones are: (1) Strictly adhere to the principle of one tax per item and implement tax refunds for double taxation; (2) To facilitate nationwide validity after one tax, taxes should be levied at the place of production or concentration in one go and not in stages; (3) The determination of what constitutes luxury goods and semi-luxury goods should accommodate the opinions of commercial organizations when each province reports; (4) The Ministry should consider the commercial situation and reconvene a Likin Abolition Conference to jointly determine the highest tax rate for semi-luxury goods and luxury goods; (5) The collection method of special taxes in each province should consult with commercial organizations in advance according to the guidelines for special taxes. This is our fourth request. The business tax rate is determined according to the implementation guidelines for the collection of business tax in each province, with the highest tax rate being two per thousand. Although each province can formulate its own flexible measures, the tax rate levied cannot be higher than the provisions of the outline, and the restrictions are extremely strict. However, Jiangsu Province levied the business registration fee in advance before the abolition of Likin, with the highest rate reaching five per thousand. This means that once Likin is abolished and the business tax is formally reformed, the tax rate will exceed the scope. If Jiangsu Province does this, it is difficult to guarantee that other provinces will not follow suit. This is our fifth request to the Ministry for correction. The first two items concern whether Likin can be thoroughly abolished, and the latter three concern the need to avoid harsh burdens when compensating for the abolition of Likin. We hereby submit our humble opinions and request the Ministry to review and approve them separately for the benefit of all. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Finance.

Letter to All Chambers of Commerce: We are writing to inform you that the government has scheduled Likin abolition for January 1, 1931, and whether the abolition can be thorough and whether the compensation can avoid disguised Likin are both important keys. If the planning is not careful, the impact will be significant. Our Chamber, in order to fulfill its duty and alleviate the suffering of merchants, submitted a proposal to the Ministry of Finance yesterday with some suggestions. We are enclosing a copy of the proposal for your review. If you believe it is reasonable, please make a joint request. If you have other opinions, please submit them to the Ministry separately. This will ensure that the long-cherished desire of merchants for Likin abolition can be realized. We are truly grateful.

租界水價問題 120

Water Price Issues in the Concession 121

Real Estate Association's Important Letter Shanghai Real Estate Association yesterday sent a letter to the Shanghai Concession Taxpayers Association of Chinese, stating, "We have received your letter of November 29th, enclosing a copy of the audit report of the Shanghai Waterworks Company's accounts and requesting our opinion. Upon review, we find that the audit was conducted through the efforts of your representatives, Mr. He Dejun, Mr. Pan Xulun, and Mr. Yu Xigen. We are deeply grateful and ask you to convey our respects and appreciation to them. As for the accounting of the 25% surcharge collected by the Shanghai Waterworks Company, we absolutely cannot approve it. Please allow us to state our reasons as follows: (1) From the principle of contract law, users have absolutely no obligation to fulfill the interest guarantee in the contract signed between the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Shanghai International Settlement and the British Shanghai Waterworks Company. The Water Company's desire to collect a surcharge is to compensate for the interest guaranteed by the Municipal Council in the current contract signed with the Water Company on March 17, 1928. Fulfilling this interest guarantee responsibility should be borne by the Municipal Council, who signed the contract and made the guarantee, and absolutely not by third-party users (i.e., customers). The Municipal Council may believe that the right to sign this contract was granted by the taxpayers, and users are taxpayers, so the interest guarantee should naturally be borne by the users. Regardless of whether users and taxpayers are two separate identities that cannot be combined into one, even if users are taxpayers, increasing the burden on taxpayers should naturally be decided by the taxpayers' meeting. Furthermore, interest guarantees should be paid by the national treasury if approved by the central government and by the municipal treasury if approved by the municipal government. This is the only principle in financial administration. There is absolutely no precedent for any industrial or commercial enterprise or public utility to charge customers for interest guarantees. Otherwise, what is the use of interest guarantees? The government's interest guarantee to enterprises is to protect investors from being unprofitable on the one hand and to protect consumers from high prices on the other hand. (2) From the principle of interest guarantees, the Shanghai Waterworks Company has no need for interest guarantees under the current circumstances. According to the principle that laws should not be retroactive mentioned in the first item, this item should not be damaged. However, people will inevitably say that this is an established contract and cannot be established before the contract signed between the Municipal Council and the Water Company is changed according to the principle that laws should not be retroactive. In reality, this is not the case. Waterworks are public utilities and monopolistic operations for the benefit of all residents. In this prosperous area, supply and demand have long been adapted, and there is absolutely no need to worry about attracting and consolidating capital. Before 1917, the Water Company was not guaranteed interest by the Municipal Council and was instead subject to price restrictions. The Water Company did not face any problems of being unsustainable. Furthermore, the reason why interest guarantees should not be borne by third-party users has been stated in the first item above. If the Municipal Council pays, this interest guarantee that increases the burden on taxpayers should be decided by the taxpayers' meeting. (3) After carefully reading the audit report, the issuance of bonus shares has greatly deviated from the principle of public utilities. Bonus shares are transformed from the Water Company's public reserve fund and distributed to shareholders. If we assume that the annual interest rate is 5%, the company has annual income, but now it has become bonus shares, and the company must have annual expenses. Calculating the current interest rate at 5%, the Water Company loses a total of 1.4% of annual interest, totaling 27,311 pounds and 4 shillings in British currency. It is unreasonable for a monopolistic waterworks company to give away its assets to shareholders. Secondly, the Water Company's A shares can be sold for about 25 pounds on the London market. Calculating at 25 pounds, the annual interest rate on the London interest rate market is about 7.2%, but this is a monopolistic operation with little need for outside investment. Its interest rate should naturally be lower than the market interest rate for various government bonds and real estate, which do not have to worry about significant losses. Thirdly, the dividend and bonus records only cover 15 years, but the average is 1.121%. The most questionable aspect is that in the two years of 1928 and 1929 under the so-called interest guarantee, shareholders' income was above 1%. Is the so-called interest guarantee of 9% guaranteeing more than 9%? Fourthly, under the so-called interest guarantee, the Water Company's expenses increased dramatically compared to under the price restriction. Even if the increase in production and consumption is maintained at the same rate, it is not in line with scientific principles. Water is not a product with many varieties. As production increases, the cost should naturally decrease. Even if prices are affected, the increase in water production should only be about 20%, while the increase in expenses is as high as 43%. It cannot be said that the Water Company is not abusing and wasting money under the so-called interest guarantee. (4) Exchange rate fluctuations are an irresistible natural disaster. The Water Company benefited from this before 1919. This time, the Water Company should suffer the loss. The Municipal Council, as the contracting party, has no need to bear the risk of this exchange rate fluctuation. This is a common principle applicable to the performance of any contract. In summary, in the current situation, the interest guarantee should be paid directly by the contracting party, the Municipal Council. In the future, the Municipal Council should revise this contract. The main points are: (1) Under the current currency system in our country, the company's capital should be calculated in silver, and the exchange rate should be the average of the last ten years. (2) Abolish the interest guarantee and restore price restrictions, and limit the interest rate. (3) All bonus shares and the property of the waterworks equipment company should be recovered and returned to the Water Company or even to the Municipal Council for the benefit of the public. Otherwise, the interest should be suspended, and the company should gradually recover them at face value. (4) Chinese directors should be added to the Water Company to supervise its operations. Since there are only foreign directors now, we are sending this letter to request your review, consideration, and adoption. Furthermore, we are extremely grateful for your hard work in the audit task.

Qian Chengxu's Opinion Guowen News Agency reported that their reporter interviewed Mr. Qian Chengxu, a member of the China Industrial Federation, yesterday to inquire about his legal opinions on the recent price increase by the Shanghai Waterworks Company. Mr. Qian replied that from a legal standpoint, there are three main parties involved in this case: the Municipal Council, the Water Company, and the users. Among the three, the users are not parties to the contract, so they cannot recognize its regulations regarding the price increase issue. The reporter asked for an explanation of the principle. Qian replied that in the past, the company's fees were calculated according to the house price, and the supply and demand relationship allowed the two parties to agree on the scope. Since the Municipal Council guaranteed the company's dividends on January 17, 1918, the Municipal Council has been in a responsible position. Therefore, at any time, if the company's income is not enough to pay its interest, the Municipal Council must pay the shortfall itself. This is because the Municipal Council guaranteed it, not the users. In short, the Municipal Council, as a party to the contract, should be responsible, and the users, who are not parties to the contract, should not bear the responsibility for the guarantee. The reporter further inquired about the legal basis for the Municipal Council's interest guarantee and approval of the price increase. Qian replied that public utilities in cities in various countries are usually managed by the municipal government. The government must promote the establishment of a company in sparsely populated areas with underdeveloped commerce and industry if its income is not enough to cover its expenses. Under these circumstances, the government can guarantee its stock interest or provide profitable goals, aiming to encourage general investment. However, after carefully examining the company's operating conditions from 1915 to 1918 (the year the Municipal Council provided the interest guarantee), its average interest had already exceeded 1.23%. Its level of development had also reached its peak. What principle did the Municipal Council use to provide a double guarantee beyond the 20-year patent? This is something I deeply disagree with. As for the approval of the price increase, I have already stated its principle. The Municipal Council, having assumed this major economic responsibility at the time, believed that it had reliable financial resources and would have special methods to provide financial support in the future. Now, without any support, it first removes its guarantee responsibility and then rashly approves the company's price increase, taking compensation for its gold price loss from the general users. This is something the Municipal Council should not have done. In short, the Municipal Council is the center of today's negotiations. From its position, the Municipal Council was able to approve the company's request to increase prices in the past, so why can't it approve the users' request to reduce prices today? Users residing in the concession have always been treated differently. Regarding this matter, the Shanghai Real Estate Association, the Concession Taxpayers Association of Chinese, and various industrial and commercial organizations can submit counter-proposals to the Municipal Council to continue their strong advocacy.

絲業請發公債之部批 122

Ministry's Approval for Issuing Public Bonds for the Silk Industry 123

The silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces had previously submitted a request to the government to issue 10 million yuan in public bonds for the silk industry in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai to provide relief. The Shanghai Silk Factory Association and the delegation of representatives from silk factories in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai received two orders of approval from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce yesterday. They are recorded below: (1) Order of approval to the Shanghai Silk Factory Association: We have received your submission regarding this case and the letter from the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan to the Ministry, which has been consulted with the Ministry of Finance for review and processing. Please be informed. 市商會徵詢各業運費意見 126

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Seeks Opinions on Freight Rates from Various Industries 127

Preparing to Submit to the Railway Freight Rate Conference The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent letters to all industries in the city, forwarded by the Municipal Government, regarding the Railway Department's consultation. The railway freight rate is extremely important. Whether the freight rate is appropriate is not only related to the prosperity and decline of the railway business, but also has a significant impact on the national economy, people's livelihood, industrial development, and commercial prosperity. The freight rates of various state-owned railways in our country have been implemented for more than ten years. Due to the changing times, the freight rates are actually no longer very applicable. In order to maintain the railway business and develop industry and commerce, it is necessary to revise the freight rates. The Ministry has now scheduled to convene a National Railway Freight Rate Conference on the 15th of next month, inviting representatives from various railways and relevant agencies such as the Ministries of Finance, Interior, Military Affairs, Agriculture, Mining, Industry, and Commerce, as well as provincial and municipal governments and local chambers of commerce, to revise the current freight rates. Therefore, we consult your government to check whether it is appropriate to send personnel to attend at that time and to first instruct the chambers of commerce under your jurisdiction to thoroughly investigate, review, and submit the production and sales of agricultural products, industries, and other goods in each place, the conditions of water and land transportation, and opinions on the railway freight rates specified to the Ministry before December 20 of this year to be used as the basis for the conference. Also instruct personnel to attend at that time to collect the benefits of broad thinking. This matter concerns the national economy and the people's livelihood. Please promptly transfer and handle it. The freight rates charged by the railway vary, and the situation of each industry is also different. It is considered that there are places that should be revised. It is better to seek opinions from each industry and submit detailed statements, and then compile and report them to the association, which is easier to obtain the main points than in a conference. We hereby send a letter to inform you and hope that you will report in detail on the current railway freight rates of your industry's goods and whether there are any improvements to be made within seven days of receiving this letter so that we can compile and forward them. This is extremely important.

金融專家論銀市意見 128

Financial Experts Discuss Silver Market Opinions 129

Saying There is No Need to Panic A reporter from the Great America Evening Post yesterday (the 1st) interviewed many foreign exchange brokers and financial experts to ask for their opinions on the silver market. They all said that there is no need to panic about the current sharp decline in silver prices. It is expected that the market will fall for a few more weeks, but unless the world economic situation continues to deteriorate and becomes more depressed than it is now, the silver market will definitely rebound. It seems that the recent drop in silver prices will not have a significant impact on the standard of living, and it is expected that the silver market will rebound in the next few days. After stabilizing for a while, it may fall again. In short, the silver market in this port is entirely dependent on the European and American markets. If the European and American economic situation improves, the silver price will definitely rise. Otherwise, if the market situation of general goods is not good, the silver price will also fall sharply. As for the cost of living in this port, it will probably be affected after the silver price falls by one or two cents. At that time, imports will decrease sharply, and prices will rise again, or even rise by about 10%.

Yesterday's Banquet for Mr. Ohtani by Five Organizations 130

The Hopes of Five Organizations

Mr. Ohtani's Response

Yesterday at 12 noon, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the Bankers' Association, the Money Exchange Association, the Shipping Association, and the Lumber Merchants' Association hosted a banquet at the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce in honor of Mr. Ohtani, a leader in American shipping and lumber industries. Over forty people attended, including Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Hu Mengjia, Qin Runqing, Zhu Yinjiang, Huang Renzhi, Shou Jingwei, Zhao Shifu, Lin Kanghou, Xu Xinliu, and Yuan Ludeng. After the meal, Yu Qiaqing, the chairman, rose and first mentioned that Mr. Ohtani had provided significant support for the establishment of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce thirty or forty years ago. At that time, he also proposed the establishment of a Sino-American joint venture bank and shipping company, but unfortunately, it did not come to fruition. However, in these thirty years, Mr. Ohtani's own shipping and lumber businesses have achieved great success. Today, he raised a toast to celebrate and hoped that everyone present would be encouraged to achieve great success in their respective businesses like Mr. Ohtani. Next, Wang Xiaolai, the chairman of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, delivered a welcome speech on behalf of the five organizations. Mr. Ohtani then gave his response. The two speeches are recorded separately as follows:

Welcome Speech by the Five Organizations: It briefly stated that Mr. Ohtani's business, particularly in lumber and shipping, has long been highly respected. He has a deep affection for the Chinese business community and has maintained close relationships for many years. It has often been heard that in his dealings with Chinese businesses over the years, involving millions of transactions, he has never experienced any unexpected losses, and no debts have ever been shortchanged. He serves as a model for businessmen. Mr. Ohtani is truly one of the most knowledgeable individuals regarding Chinese business conditions. The prosperity of commerce between the two countries must be based on mutual trust between the merchants of both nations. While Mr. Ohtani's success in Chinese commerce is due to various advantages, his spirit of mutual trust is undoubtedly one of the greatest reasons for his success. Our association not only hopes that Mr. Ohtani will maintain this spirit but also hopes to disseminate this concept widely among American merchants in China and, upon his return home, to contribute significantly to the American authorities. In doing so, Sino-American commerce will undoubtedly usher in a new era. The biggest obstacle to the U.S. State Department's hesitation in abolishing extraterritoriality in China is the concern that the abolition of extraterritoriality might affect the protection of American businesses in China. If Mr. Ohtani can use his decades of commercial experience in China to sincerely appeal to the American authorities, making them understand that Chinese merchants are the most honest and trustworthy, then the anxiety that the abolition of extraterritoriality would affect commercial security will naturally dissipate. Mr. Ohtani, at the advanced age of nearly ninety, has traveled across the ocean. If he can make this great contribution, it would be a lasting memorial in the history of Sino-American trade. We cannot help but have great expectations. Secondly, when we look back at Mr. Ohtani's history of success, it is indeed due to the words "perseverance and determination." This is especially a good model for us in China, where industrial and commercial undertakings are still in the process of construction. Even if we consider the origin of Mr. Ohtani's shipping business, he initially suffered significant losses because he entrusted others to transport lumber. He then reluctantly purchased a small, three-hundred-ton ship and transported it himself, eventually expanding to specialize in lumber transportation, leading to the establishment of the now-famous Ohtani Steamship Company. There is an ancient saying in our country: "The success of nine-ren starts with a pile of earth." How true that is. Recalling that our country had a shipping company called China Merchants Steam Navigation Company several years ago, which had three ships, the "China," "Nile," and "Nanjing," sailing between China and the United States, it failed and ceased operations after only a few years. Compared to Mr. Ohtani, who accumulated inch by inch from a small three-hundred-ton vessel to build a world-renowned shipping company, we are truly ashamed. Further, our country's merchants are known for being honest in their words, but they lack the experience in managing large-scale businesses. There is an ancient saying in our country: "The stones from other mountains can be used to polish jade," which means that friends have the obligation to exchange knowledge. Therefore, on the occasion of welcoming Mr. Ohtani today, we ask him, as a good friend and a senior, to share all his business experiences throughout his life with the financial and shipping circles present today, so that our organizations can use them as an aid to improving their businesses. His generous gift to our country's business community will be substantial indeed.

Mr. Ohtani's Response: Before I begin my collective response, there are a few words I must declare: I do not feel that I am associating with people from a foreign country when I am at your association today. I feel as if I am talking with old acquaintances from my own country. Based on this special feeling, it is only appropriate for me to address everyone as "old friends." Chairman Wang mentioned various points regarding Sino-American relations in his welcome speech. I am very willing to respond with simple and sincere words: I am willing to do my best in my remaining years to benefit China and its people. I can guarantee the business credit of the Chinese people. I have been doing business in China for decades and have never suffered any losses. Friendship is essential to mankind. If mankind has no friendship, how boring would life be? With the spirit of love, friendship, and trustworthiness of the Chinese people, coupled with unity of purpose and concerted efforts, I dare say that in twenty or thirty years, China will surely become the world's leading power and will naturally hold the reins of the business community of all countries. Please do not consider this flattery or an empty promise. This observation of mine comes from a sincere realization. Just as I have been away from Shanghai for three years and have returned to this place, the development of Shanghai has already leaped forward. But this hope must have a prerequisite issue, that is, to permanently end the war. I know that with the concerted efforts of everyone present here, there will be no more wars in China forever. Because I love it so much, I cannot help but speak so earnestly, so I add this point as an aside. I also visited various ministers during my trip to your country's capital and had a long conversation with Chairman Chiang. What I said was the same as what I said to you today. Chairman Chiang also told me that he deeply believed in what I said and would do his best to make it a reality. I know that in twenty or thirty years, I will meet with you again. At that time, you will say that the hopes Mr. Ohtani expressed in the past have all become reality today. Wouldn't that be great?

Ministry Approval for Exemption of Silk Reeling Tax for Zhejiang-Huzhou Silk Merchants 131

This newspaper has repeatedly reported on the requests from Zhejiang-Huzhou silk merchant representatives Pan Run and Diao Zuolan to the Ministry of Finance for tax exemption on goods passing through various regions. It is now known that the Ministry of Finance has approved the silk reeling tax exemption, the original text of which is as follows:

Received the petition stating that Shanghai has a large inventory of raw silk and reeled silk, which is restricted by heavy taxes, resulting in limited commercial transportation in Shanghai. If tax exemption is allowed for imports, then the sale of raw silk and reeled silk in Shanghai can be promoted, and the silk workers in Huzhou can gradually resume work. The situation is indeed true. At present, the abolition of local duties is imminent. In order to promote domestic products and consider both sides, the Ministry hereby approves a temporary measure before the actual abolition of local duties. All Huzhou merchants who purchase raw silk and reeled silk from Shanghai should obtain certificates from the Wuxing Silk Weaving Association. After verification by various regions, if the goods match the certificate, tax exemption shall be granted. In addition to instructing the Jiangsu Financial Commissioner, the Zhejiang Department of Finance, to comply with this order, please submit a sample of the certificate form adopted by the association to the Ministry for record and compliance. This approval is hereby issued.

Japanese Chargé d'Affaires Protests Construction of Zhenru Radio Station 132

The international radio station built by the Ministry of Communications in Zhenru has been completed and is scheduled to open on the 6th of this month. It was recently learned that this matter has suddenly aroused unreasonable interference from Japan. According to personnel from the Japanese Embassy in Shanghai, during the Duan government era in the seventh year of the Republic of China, a Shuangqiao Radio Station contract was signed with Japan. This contract stipulated that Japan had exclusive rights to China's construction of radio stations. The Japanese believe that the Ministry of Communications' order to the United States for materials and loans to build the Zhenru radio station violates the old Shuangqiao contract and have expressed their protest. The Japanese Chargé d'Affaires, Shigemitsu Aoi, had previously submitted a protest letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Because the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not yet replied, the protest was continued yesterday.

Mr. and Mrs. You and Zhang Reconcile 133

Wang Yiting and Yu Zhizhai exerted their utmost to mediate. A one-time subsidy of 5,000 yuan was given to compensate You Yahao's losses. Zhang Nai sent a letter of apology and assumed future alimony responsibilities. You Yahao's lawsuit has not yet been withdrawn.

The bigamous marriage case between You Yahao and Zhang Nai has caused a sensation in Shanghai since it occurred, attracting widespread attention. Now, with the utmost mediation of Mr. Wang Yiting, Pastor Yu Zhizhai, and others, and the letter from Mr. Wang Yiting and others to invite Ms. You's father, Gan Chen, to Shanghai, the matter has taken a sharp turn. As of the 30th of last month, both parties began discussing settlement terms. Zhang Nai himself voluntarily subsidized Ms. You with 5,000 yuan for expenses such as childbirth and litigation. Future living expenses would be subsidized at 30 yuan per month by Zhang Nai's elder brother, Yu Baoyuan, until Zhang Nai obtains employment. If Zhang Nai earns a salary of 150 yuan or less after obtaining employment, 60 yuan per month will be subsidized. If it exceeds 150 yuan, it will be increased accordingly. Zhang Ding formally sent a letter of apology to Ms. You's parents. Once the conditions proposed by Zhang Nai are fully fulfilled, Ms. You will withdraw the lawsuit from the court and resume cohabitation, with both parties reconciling as husband and wife. The settlement terms on You Yahao's side are entirely presided over by You's father, Gan Chen, and You Yahao has not been involved in the matter from beginning to end. However, You Yahao respects the mediation of the mediators and the opinions of her father and has therefore expressed her approval. However, as of today, Zhang Nai has only fulfilled the apology to Ms. You Yahao and her parents. As for the subsidized 5,000 yuan, Zhang Nai has raised it and stored it in a certain bank but has not handed it over, stating that it must wait until Zhang's conditions are fully fulfilled before the lawsuit can be formally withdrawn. You's father returned to his hometown yesterday. Ms. You and her son have been unwell in recent days and are accompanied by medicine stoves and teapots. The original letter of apology from Zhang Nai and the original certificate of the witness are transcribed below:

Zhang Nai's Original Letter: I respectfully address my esteemed parents-in-law. Since your daughter married me, she has served her mother-in-law dutifully, managed the household diligently and thriftily, and provided deep inner assistance. The relationship has been extremely harmonious. Now, due to my temporary confusion, I have caused a bigamous marriage dispute and legal proceedings. There are places in my court testimony that offend your daughter and do not conform to the facts. I have now realized my mistake and feel deeply ashamed. I sincerely express my apology to my esteemed parents-in-law and your daughter, and request your daughter's forgiveness so that we can remain husband and wife as before. In the future, we will always maintain harmony. I will fulfill my obligation to support your daughter and abide by the law without changing course midway. All household expenses, childbirth expenses, litigation expenses, etc., advanced by your daughter will be reimbursed by me with 5,000 yuan. The living expenses of your daughter and son should be borne by me forever. It is agreed that before I obtain employment, I will temporarily subsidize your daughter and son with 30 yuan per month. After I find employment, if the salary is 150 yuan or less, I will pay 60 yuan per month. If it exceeds 150 yuan, it will be increased accordingly, guaranteed by my elder brother. All the items stored at my elder sister's place will still be returned by my elder sister as before. I earnestly request my parents-in-law and your daughter to be generous and allow the civil and criminal lawsuits to be withdrawn, so that I may be grateful for the rest of my life. I respectfully wish you good health. Your son-in-law, Zhang Nai, bows on the 30th day of the 11th month of the 19th year.

Movement to Resist Japanese and Return Opium 134

A German ship was found to be carrying opium worth over one million. On the morning of the 20th of last month, the Jianghai Customs discovered one hundred boxes of opium weighing 19,400 pounds and worth one million yuan on the German cargo ship "Kroesso" at a pier next to the China Merchants Bureau's warehouse in Pudong. The opium was being smuggled by the Japanese, as reported earlier. It is now learned that the smuggling Japanese are using a lot of money to vigorously lobby in all directions, hoping to return the original goods. The Japanese authorities are also trying to find a way. The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association learned of this matter. Due to the seriousness of the case, the Association is determined to exert all its efforts to resist the destruction of the drugs and thoroughly investigate the smugglers. In addition to investigating the actual situation to carry out the resistance, a special letter was sent to the Director of the Ministry of Finance and the Central Anti-Opium Committee, requesting that the opium be burned as soon as possible and that the personnel involved be investigated and the handling process be announced to the public to dispel doubts and emphasize the prohibition of opium. The original letter is excerpted as follows:

Dear Sirs, It has been found that the Shanghai newspapers of November 21 carried reports that the Jianghai Customs discovered a large amount of opium on the German cargo ship "Kroesso," amounting to more than 19,400 pounds and worth more than one million yuan. A confidential letter from the shipowner to the opium customs was found. Researching the sentences in the letter is sufficient to prove that the smugglers of the opium are Japanese. That country may file a protest. The opium is currently stored in the Jianghai Customs awaiting disposal. The foreign media also published similar reports on the 22nd. It has been found that foreign drugs have harmed our country for a century, killing compatriots, destroying production, and having a huge impact. Recently, the Jianghai Customs has repeatedly seized large quantities of drugs coming to China, and the quantity has been larger than ever before. The scale of the organization and the strictness of the planning are evident. It has recently been learned that the Japanese smugglers of opium are using huge sums of money to collude with corrupt officials and traveling between Beijing and Shanghai, vigorously lobbying in the hope of returning the drugs in order to achieve their conspiracy to poison China, and that a gang of people who are willing to sell their country are even more profit-oriented and are running errands for the Japanese in order to achieve the purpose of transporting the drugs. It has been found that Japanese smuggling of large quantities of opium has always been under the pretext of transporting it to Dalian to manufacture anesthetic drugs, but in reality, it is transported to Shanghai. Unfortunately, it was discovered by the customs, and they used this as an excuse to seek its return. Even if it is actually transported to Dalian to be made into anesthetic drugs, will not our compatriots still be poisoned? Even a three-foot child knows their trick of deceiving themselves and others. The evidence of this illegal smuggling is clear, but the Japanese are still trying to rely on money and diplomacy to coerce and lure our country's authorities. The danger of their intentions has long been seen by the people of the country. Our Association has been entrusted by the people to resist drugs as its duty, and it is difficult to remain silent in the face of this dark disaster that will destroy the country and exterminate the race. It is determined to completely eliminate it. It has previously sent letters to the Jianghai Customs Supervisor and Tax Commissioner to express its opinion and request that the drugs be burned as soon as possible, but it has not been implemented. If there are any greedy and lawless people who are willing to collude with the Japanese, our Association will sound the drums and attack them. If there are any who are upright and not afraid of public opinion, who are working for the welfare of the people and are not tempted or coerced by profit, our Association swears to be a backing. It is hereby requested that the Jianghai Customs be instructed to immediately propose the burning of the opium in order to prevent abuses, thoroughly investigate the persons involved in this case, and negotiate with the countries concerned to report the facts of the case to all the people of the country and the League of Nations. It is hoped that this will be investigated and handled.

Startling Number of Car Accidents 136

Over ten thousand in eleven months. The Great America Evening News said that the number of vehicle accidents in the two concessions in this city last month was so high and the disasters were so severe that it can be said to be the highest of the year. A total of 1,134 accidents occurred in the Public Concession and the French Concession, killing 21 and injuring 372. Among them, only 160 occurred in the French Concession, killing 6 and injuring more than 50. All the others occurred in the Public Concession. In total, more than 10,053 vehicle accidents have occurred in the Public Concession in the eleven months of this year, which is more than the 9,692 accidents in the whole year of last year. It is more by more than 360 accidents, so it is expected that the total number of accidents in the eleven months of this year will exceed last year by more than 1,000, which is truly an alarming number. Also, a total of 131 people died in vehicle accidents and 3,719 were injured in the eleven months of this year, while only 141 died and 3,457 were injured in the whole year of last year.

Mortar Explosion Kills One and Injures Two 139

The tragic situation of workers in the arsenal. At about 2:00 p.m. yesterday, Han Qingtai, a patrolling police officer from the Gaochangmiao police station in the second district of the Nanshi Public Security Bureau, saw a group of people watching a corpse covered in injuries at the entrance of Lane 53 on Longhua Road. Someone was taking care of it by the roadside. Officer Han immediately stepped forward and asked why the deceased had died on the road. Songhu Road and Xiangzha Road Both Start Construction Today 141

Songhu Road in this city was originally divided into two sections, north and south. The south section starts from Ningguo Road and ends at Kongjiang Road, and the north section starts from Xiangyin Road and ends at Jiangwan Stadium. The two sections are not connected, making transportation very inconvenient. It is now learned that the Municipal Public Works Bureau is scheduled to send workers today to start construction from Xiangyin Road in both directions to connect the road. The width of the road is set at 30 meters, and the 10-meter wide road surface will be built first. Also, the Municipal Public Works Bureau originally had a plan to build a road called Xiangzha Road from Diswei Road to the intersection of Songhu Road and Xiangyin Road. The planned width from Diswei Road to Shajing Port is 15.03 meters, and the width from Shajing Port to Xiangyin Road is 35 meters. The 10-meter wide road surface will also begin construction today.

Ships Not Allowed to Anchor at Underwater Cable Crossing in Huangpu River 142

The electric company installs signs. The Shanghai Chinese Electric Company and the Pudong Electric Company have laid a submarine cable in the Huangpu River from about 280 meters southwest of the Shanghai Arsenal to the northwest end of the China Wharf, and from the riverside wharf east of the Jiangnan Shipyard in Shanghai to the northwest end of the Pudong Coal Industry Public Stack, respectively. The project has been completed and submitted to the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, which issued a notice together with the Public Security and Port Affairs Bureaus prohibiting ships from anchoring at the river crossing of the underwater cable to prevent damage. The company also followed the instructions of the Public Utilities Bureau to plan and install clear signs in Chinese with the eight characters (Electric Cable Crossing Prohibited Anchoring), each character being two English feet long and wide, and in English with the two words (Cable Crossing), each letter being eight inches wide and two English feet long. It also entrusted the Dongfang Nianhong Company to manufacture two Nianhong (Neon) lamps, one to be set up at the underwater cable on the southwest side of the Shanghai Arsenal and the other at the northwest end of the Pudong Coal Industry Public Stack, to emit light day and night, and the installation will be completed within the day. In addition, two white-painted T-shaped wooden boards were made, with the Chinese and English warning words painted on them in red paint. One was installed at the riverside wharf in Shanghai and the other at the underwater cable at the northwest end of the China Wharf in Pudong, and electric lights were installed around them to be powered on at night. Both signs are erected on ocean pine poles and planted in the river near the dredging line so that ships can pay more attention to them. In addition, boats are hired to patrol the river day and night, and warning signs are also installed on the boats. If a ship is found to be stopped and anchored, it will be stopped. In addition, notices are printed and staff are sent to distribute them to the ships in the river every other day and mailed to the import and export ship schedules published in the newspapers to urge them to pay attention. The maintenance of the cable is so thorough that no damage should occur.

Sudden Drop in Posted Exchange Rate 143

The posted exchange rates in this city have been gradually decreasing in recent days. A week ago, one yuan could be exchanged for ten jiao plus 380 or 390 wen, equivalent to more than eleven jiao and four fen. Copper coins could be exchanged for 2,820 or 2,830 wen. However, the exchange rate has suddenly decreased for no reason. Yesterday, the posted exchange rate on the market was only ten jiao plus 260 or 245 wen, equivalent to eleven jiao, and copper coins were only 2,700 wen, which aroused public attention. The main reason for the increase in silver dollars and the sharp decrease in copper coins is purely because there were more exports last month, resulting in insufficient turnover of circulating funds in the market.

Recent News from the Tongji Alumni Association 144

Dr. Paulun and Dr. Behrendt, the founders of the National Wusong Tongji University, and Mr. Yuan Guanrun, who worked hardest to maintain the school after its dissolution during the European War, have all passed away one after another. For the sake of honoring virtue and repaying merit, Tongji alumni planned to erect statues and monuments in their memory. The 46th meeting was held on October 4th of this year. Alumni present included Wu Zijing, Shen Keng, Wang Chuanxi, Cao Xing, Wang Taizhen, Guo Zhijing, Shi Demin, Zhang Boyu, Hu Jiayan, Ding Junda, Xu Shaoyu, Xi Fuquan, Yang Zhuofan, Jin Ruyuan, Xue Zhihao, Liang Zhiyan, Wang Yongqing, Cai Qishu, Dun Dexin, and others. They discussed methods for commemorating Dr. Paulun and Dr. Behrendt. Six resolutions were passed as follows: (1) In addition to commemorating Dr. Paulun and Dr. Behrendt, a monument will also be erected for Mr. Yuan Guanrun. (2) The estimated total cost for the three memorial towers is approximately 600 yuan, which will be the standard for fundraising. (3) Donation amounts will be divided into three categories: 2 yuan, 5 yuan, and 10 yuan, chosen freely by alumni. (4) Mr. Wu Zijing is publicly recommended to be responsible for collecting donations and reporting the amounts at each dinner gathering. (5) All matters related to the construction of the monuments will be handled by the Alumni Association's Executive Committee in conjunction with the principal of the alma mater. (6) Notify all alumni associations to solicit donations to help make this happen. It is heard that alumni in various places have been actively recognizing and donating, and the collection address is No. 95 Wuding Road (between Hart Road and Jiaozhou Road). So says Mr. Wu Zijing.

Zhenjiang Boatmen Are Very

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiangshun Steamer was arriving at Zhenjiang around 2:00 AM the day before yesterday (the 1st). Lu Yunxi's Wife Files for Divorce 147

Debate Concluded; Awaiting Judgment Lu Yunxi, a native of Songjiang who previously ran the two tabloids ("Ah Yao Wo Xin") and ("Crazy Wind"), was recently sued in the civil court by his wife, Lu Jicheng Ying, through a lawyer. The lawsuit alleged that Lu engaged in prostitution and gambling, was addicted to opium, and neglected the plaintiff, making cohabitation unbearable. The court ordered both parties to attempt reconciliation. Yesterday, a continued hearing was held. The defendant's lawyer stated that the plaintiff had never come to reconcile after the court order, and that the defendant opposed the divorce and requested the court to order the plaintiff to retrieve all her clothing and belongings and resume cohabitation. At this point, the plaintiff, Ji Cheng Ying, asked the court to observe that the defendant, Lu Yunxi, looked entirely like a "split-bill" type who had swindled women out of over a thousand yuan, which he had not returned a single cent. Furthermore, the defendant had published the woman's photograph in the newspaper with malicious words, deliberately insulting her. Given the complete breakdown of the marital relationship, cohabitation was impossible, and there was no hope of reconciliation. She requested a ruling and submitted the two newspapers in question for examination. Lu Yunxi claimed that the news was published by newspaper reporters and had nothing to do with him. Ji Cheng Ying responded that even if the news was published by reporters, the photograph belonged to the defendant, so why was it published in the newspaper? Was this not a deliberate attempt to damage her reputation? Judge Gong, the presiding judge, declared the debate concluded and the case would be heard for judgment.

Burying the Money in the Dirt

Detectives Capture Two People in Succession

Cao Shi, the mistress of the Cao Shuntai rickshaw company at No. 2992 Haining Road, recently reported that a gang of bandits sent a threatening letter demanding 1,500 yuan. They instructed her to deliver the money at 9:00 PM the night before last to a lane next to the Chenyi Hotel on Youheng Road, where there was a telephone pole with a red paper attached. She was to bury the money in the dirt under the pole without fail. Cao Shi immediately reported this to the police station, who dispatched detectives to guard the location as scheduled. Case of Abduction of a Newlywed Woman 152

Plotting to Sell Her as a Prostitute After Sexual Assault

Chen Honghai and Others Are Detained

Jin Shoufu, 22 years old, a native of Yancheng who lives at No. 14, 30 Jian, Beiyinghua Lane, Laobosheng Road, in western Shanghai, works as a night-soil collector. He has always been poor and recently, in August of this year, married a woman from his hometown named A Bao through a matchmaker. A Bao is only 15 years old. After the marriage, the couple was very loving. Jin was often on the boat, while A Bao worked in a factory. Recently, Chen Honghai, who lives at No. 16 next door, and his cohabiting woman, Chen Shi, noting that A Bao was beautiful, young, and weak, colluded to abduct her. On the 25th of last month, Chen Shi and Chen Honghai devised a plan to lure A Bao to the North Railway Station under the pretext of going to the theater. They entered a small hotel and rented a room. A Bao, seeing the situation, became suspicious and repeatedly tried to leave, but was forcibly prevented by the woman and sexually assaulted by Chen Honghai for three consecutive nights. During the day, a man named Zhang Shaolin came to the hotel to secretly discuss matters with Chen and the woman repeatedly. Later, they suddenly took A Bao to a certain brothel on Sixth Avenue. They sat there briefly for an hour on the evening of the 28th, and then Chen, Zhang, and A Bao went to a hotel on Fifth Avenue and rented a room. At this time, A Bao realized that she was being sold and pretended not to know. She took the opportunity to find out that Zhang had introduced her to the brothel for a price of 200 yuan, which was to be finalized the next day. A Bao was greatly alarmed and ran out to report the incident to the police on the 29th. They arrested Chen Honghai, Chen Shi, and Zhang Shaolin together and took them to the police station. After the head detective questioned them, he dispatched detectives to investigate. A Bao's husband, Jin Shoufu, was looking for her when he suddenly learned that she had been arrested and taken to the police station. Because the area was within the Chinese territory, Jin reported the incident to the Sixth District Branch Office, which was relayed to the Sixth District Police Department by Inspector Su. Director Ren of the district received the report and dispatched squad leader Liu Shaoqing and others from the detective team to the police station to bring back the four suspects together. After Director Ren questioned them, Jin Shoufu confessed that he was 22 years old, from Yancheng, and lived at No. 14, 30 Jian, and worked as a night-soil collector. Jin A Bao confessed that she was 15 years old, from the same place, and was abducted, sexually assaulted, and sold as described above. Chen Honghai confessed that he was 23 years old, from Ningbo, lived at No. 16, 30 Jian, and worked in a factory. He admitted to sexually assaulting and selling A Bao. Zhang Shaolin confessed that he was 21 years old, from Dachang, lived in Caoxiebang, and worked as a small worker. He claimed that Chen borrowed a robe from him for 3 yuan and 6 jiao to pay for the hotel, and falsely claimed that he knew nothing about the sale of A Bao. His other words were also very cunning. The woman, Chen Shi, confessed that she was 21 years old, from Changzhou, lived at No. 16, 30 Jian, and worked in the Fifth Cotton Mill. She admitted to abducting and selling A Bao and stated that her husband's name was Chen Hongfa. After hearing the confessions, Director Ren, believing that the case involved collusion to design the abduction of a newlywed woman, sexual assault, and intention to sell her as a prostitute, which was extremely illegal, dispatched detectives to summon Chen Hongfa to the case. Yesterday, a special document was prepared and sent to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

A Tianjin Friend Describes the Achievements of the Haijing Wool Weaving Industry 153

A Tianjin friend describes the rapid progress of the products of the Haijing Wool Weaving Factory. The following is a record: In the Chinese machine wool weaving industry, the Qinghe Ni Ge Factory was established in Beijing 20 years ago. However, due to business failure, no one has continued to operate it for a long time. At present, only the wool weaving factory operated by the American Haijing Foreign Firm in Tianjin can be called a rare survivor. Originally, the Haijing Foreign Firm specialized in managing wool weaving machines. Six years ago, due to the smooth export of Chinese carpets to the United States, it established its own factory on Hai Da Road. The firm purchased wool, spun it itself, dyed it, and still used hand-weaving. The scale of the operation is large and is the leading carpet factory in the country. The machine for spinning warp yarn was specially ordered from the United States and is large, not even found in the United States. Since Chinese carpets have had this warp yarn winding machine, the products have improved compared to before, and sales have been maintained. This year, the price of gold has soared, and the value of imported wool textiles has increased, while domestic demand is increasing day by day. The owner of Haijing, in view of this, established a machine weaving factory in Xikai two years ago. Machine-made bed blankets and carriage blankets are already being sold to the United States, bringing glory to Chinese industry. This year, the factory has further advanced to weaving clothing wool, and its products are as pure and strong as imported goods, but the value is half the price. Although the factory uses foreign guests, all raw materials and labor are Chinese. The specialized talents are also Chinese experts who have studied abroad, so its products should be regarded as domestic goods. This time, the Beijing-Liaoning through train needed new bed blankets because the old ones were worn out. It ordered 500 bed blankets from the foreign firm because the firm's products were excellent and the prices were cheap. Now, the bed blankets of the first-class sleeper cars of the Beijing-Liaoning through train have been replaced with new ones.

Jiangxi Representatives Arrive in Shanghai to Beg for Relief 159

A Heartbreaking Letter About the Jiangxi Disaster

Yesterday, two representatives from Jiangxi, Lu Fang and Wang Mingxuan, personally arrived at the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Association to beg for relief. The Chinese and Western general secretaries met with them and stated that 24 counties in Jiangxi Province had suffered from natural disasters, and 60 counties had suffered from wind, insect, water, drought, and banditry. The disaster area was extremely wide, and the disaster situation was beyond description. Not only was there no harvest, but there was no home to return to. The weather was already cold, and there were no clothes to wear. Living in deep water and scorching fire, they did not hesitate to travel far to ask for sufficient relief so that millions of lives would not be left to fill gullies and ditches. They also presented a letter from Chairman Wang of the Provincial Relief Association, Yin Xiyuan, which was truly heartbreaking. It is copied as follows: "Jiangxi Province has unfortunately suffered repeated disasters. Last year, famine struck, and wind and insects ravaged the area. In addition, banditry has turned villages into ruins, fields into desolate places, and the countryside into thorny bushes. Corpses are piled in ditches, hurting the hearts of the old and weak. Looking to the end of the road, it is unbearable to witness the wandering children. The orphans are helpless, and the starving are pitiful. Hoping for relief and rehabilitation to usher in a paradise, official documents have been exchanged to aid those disaster victims. Although the heart is willing, the strength is lacking. A drop in the bucket can gather into a river, and united will can become a city. Hoping that the soil will become a mountain, who would have thought that the startled panting had not ceased and the red flames flared up again? Southern Jiangxi, such as Ganxian, Ji'an, Xingguo, Huichang, Ninggang, Yongxin, and Ruijin. Eastern Jiangxi, such as Yiyang, Guangfeng, Yushan, and Guixi. Western Jiangxi, such as Pingxiang, Yichun, Fenyi, and Wan載. Northern Jiangxi, such as Xiushui, Fuliang, Leping, and Lin陽, dozens of counties have suffered such tragic disasters that it is unbearable to speak of. Killing, arson, and looting. The strong are scattered, and the weak remain. The rich are impoverished, and the poor die. Groaning and awaiting death, they are all innocent people. Piled up in heaps, they are all green phosphorescent bones. The weeping boats and women drift, where can they rely? The elderly are sadly desperate at the door. Where can they hide from the continuous beacon fires? Surrounded by the sound of horns, the world is full of man-eating wolves and tigers. Who has no parents? Who has no wife and children? Seeing this cruelty, how can we not be saddened? Moreover, the frost and snow are coming soon. We must plan ahead, how can we allow this to be delayed?" It is heard that the association has exhausted all its resources in raising funds for the Northwest disasters in recent years and is currently lacking special funds for Jiangxi relief. In view of this situation, they are extremely anxious and eagerly hope that all sectors, if they have compassion for the people of Jiangxi, will quickly and generously donate to be sent to the disaster area to save them from their imminent crisis.

The Radical Advancement of the Zhejiang-Shanghai Coastal Shipping Industry 160

The number of ships in the province and their categories: Zhejiang, due to its environmental conditions, is not affected by military affairs, so its construction is the best in the country. Zhejiang's coastal affairs have been handled with particular success. The latest news from the Zhejiang-Shanghai shipping industry is recorded in general terms as follows:

Shenjiamen Opens a New Route Shenjiamen is an important port area on the east coast of Zhejiang. In recent years, the number of marine products transported to Shanghai and other places has been increasing day by day. For the needs of the business community in the port, the Sanbei Company, controlled by Yu Qiaqing, built a new-style oil engine commercial ship with a deadweight of 1,000 tons in Shanghai at a cost of 140,000 taels for the use of the Shenjiamen route. This ship has been launched and is currently being equipped with passenger seats and will be able to start its scheduled service in early next month. The Sanbei Company has scheduled a daily service along the route, including Wanzhou and Zhoushan. It is heard that the transportation authorities have decided to establish a telegraph office in Shenjiamen for the convenience of shipping companies.

Zhoushan is Designated as a Fishing Irrigation Area The Zhejiang authorities have designated Zhoushan as a fishing port area to develop the province's fishing industry. The area designated by the provincial authorities is from Changtu Port in Dinghai to Shenjiamen. A fishing and experimental site has also been established. Sanmen Bay has also been designated as a fishing port. It is forbidden for Japanese fishing boats to enter the designated area. The Navy Department has been consulted to send a warship from December 1st to protect fishing boats and suppress pirates.

Construction of Twenty Public Ports The Zhejiang Shipping Administration Bureau, in order to develop coastal and inland river shipping, has not only chartered China Merchants' civilian ships and added money to the upper reaches of the Qianjiang River, but is now building twenty public wharf docks for steamships in various ports such as Kanmen, Zhenhai, Zhoushan, Shenjiamen, and Wuxing in eastern Zhejiang. Technician Chen and twenty surveyors have been sent to measure and map the locations before construction.

The Daily Prosperity of the Shanghai Route The Shanghai-Ningbo route has been jointly operated by four companies this year, with an agreed annual amount of 800,000 yuan, which is shared by the four companies, with Ningshao receiving the largest amount and Taikoo receiving the smallest. As for the Shanghai route, the number of passengers coming and going is increasing day by day, and this year is even better than last year. Ningshao has always been in the first place. This year, the Sanbei Company will renovate the Ningxing route, and the number of passengers taking it is increasing day by day. It is driving alongside Ningshao. It is found that in the eleven months from January to the present, the total number of passenger tickets received by the ship is 260,000 yuan, plus 470,000 jiao in small money. China Merchants has fewer passengers than the other four companies. However, according to statistics, the annual revenue of the four companies from passenger tickets is at least 1,100,000 yuan.

The Number of Ships Currently in Zhejiang There are more ships from other provinces in the Zhejiang coastal area. After a thorough investigation, as of now, there are a total of 75,055 ships, including 20 coastal ships, 78 inland river ships, 4,443 commercial ships, 183 steamship tugboats, 23 speedboats, 62 music boats, 7,365 fishing boats, 2,730 agricultural boats, 5,477 port handling boats, 60 ferry boats, 968 tugboats, 316 public boats, 4 lifeboats, 232 Jiangbei boats, and 95 screw boats.

The Detained Batch of Tobacco Leaves is Released 161

Shipment to Shanghai Begins Today Henan Tobacco Leaves, a Major Production Commodity, After the Retreat of Feng's Army, Tobacco Merchants in this Port Began to Carry Money to Henan to Collect and Transport the Goods to Shanghai for Resale to Various Places in Southeast Asia. However, the First Batch of Tobacco Leaves Out of the Province, Valued at Over One Million Yuan, was Detained During Loading. Shanghai Merchants Repeatedly Appealed, and Yesterday They Finally Received News of its Release. The Truth of the Detention: It Was Found that the Total Number of Tobacco Leaves Purchased from Xuchang, Henan by Shanghai Tobacco Merchants Reached 30,000 Pieces, Valued at 1.1 Million Yuan. In Mid-last Month, After the End of the Military Affairs in Central Henan, the Goods were Ordered to be Transported. They Were Transferred from the Pinghan Road to Hankou, and then by Yangtze River Ship to Shanghai. However, When the Huge Amount of Tobacco Leaves was Shipped from Xuchang, Taxes Were Paid as Usual, and When the Goods Arrived in Hankou, Xu Shaosong, a Member of the Two Lake Tobacco Tax Bureau, Reported to the Hankou Customs that the Taxes Paid When They Were Shipped from Xuchang Were Collected by Tax Officials Dispatched by Feng Yuxiang, and the National Army Found it Difficult to Acknowledge This. The Goods Were Immediately Detained and Not Allowed to be Transferred. All 30,000 Pieces of Tobacco Leaves Were Detained.

Merchants' Appeals When Shanghai Tobacco Merchants Received the News, They Reported that the Value of the Goods was Very Large, and Once They Were Blocked, the Losses Would be Huge. They Immediately Reported to the Tobacco Association and Sent a Telegram to the Hankou and Wuhan Authorities, Stating that Merchants Paid Taxes in Accordance with Regulations and There Was Nothing Inappropriate, and They Could Not Affect the Merchants Because of Political Relations. Moreover, the Principal Was at Stake and it was Difficult to Block for a Long Time. On One Hand, They Sent Personnel to Hankou to Ask the Provincial Government to Release the Goods, and on the Other Hand, They Asked Yu Zhiqin and Others in Shanghai to Send a Telegram to Chairman He Xuezhu of the Hubei Province to Order the Garrison Command to Release the Huge Amount of Tobacco Leaves Detained from Henan Province. Telegrams Were Sent in Succession for Half a Month, and It Was Not Until Yesterday that There Were Results.

Hubei Province Allowed Release Hubei Provincial Government Chairman He Chenjun Replied to Shanghai Yesterday, Stating that He Had Collected Various Official Documents and Telegrams and, in Accordance with the Application of the Shanghai Tobacco Industry Association and Yu Qiaolao, Ordered the Relevant Authorities to Re-examine the Tax Payment Procedures. As They Were in Compliance, He Had Forwarded the Relevant Documents of this Case to the Wuhan Garrison Command, Asking it to Approve the Release of the Large Amount of Henan Tobacco Leaves Detained by the Next Day. The Detained Tobacco Leaves Can be Shipped to Shanghai, Which is a Major Transportation Business for the Shipping Industry. Various Chinese and Foreign Commercial Ships in this Port are Competing for Loading, as the Freight Alone Costs Tens of Thousands of Dollars. British and Japanese Shipping Companies are Even More Eager to Load. It Was Heard Yesterday that the Tobacco Merchants in this Port Have Decided that the Goods Will be Transported by Chinese Ships and Have Contacted the Sanbei Company to Arrange for the Bureau to Send Ships to Load the Goods to Shanghai and Distribute a Part to the China Merchants Bureau for Loading. The Shipment Will Begin Today, and the Detention Storm Has Been Resolved Peacefully.

The coffin department of the Tongren Fuyuan Main Hall in this city uses a special large truck to collect daily from the north and south cities, as well as Pudong and Shanghai West, the poor and sick who died in various hospitals and were unable to afford burial, beggars who died, and abandoned children's corpses by the roadside, etc. Last month, it collected a total of 113 large coffins and 184 small coffins.
